       <div id="content">
        <div id="content-1-topic">
         <article class="post">
          <div class="post-holder">
           <a class="less show-less-btn show_less_article_text" href="#">
            Show Less
           </a>
           <div id="topic-image-holder">
            <a href="" id="jTopicImage_1_src" target="_blank">
             <img class=" jTopicImage jTopicImageBig" data-searched="0" data-topic-id="10565718" data-topic-title="Mean Girls" id="jTopicImage_1" src=""/>
             <span class="no-copyright wait-to-display">
              
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div id="topic-article">
            <div id="main-topic-news">
            </div>
            <p>
             <i>
              <b>
               Mean Girls
              </b>
             </i>
             is a 2004 American teen comedy film directed by Mark Waters and written by Tina Fey. The film is based in part on Rosalind Wiseman's non-fiction book
             <i>
              Queen Bees and Wannabes
             </i>
             , which describes female high school social cliques and the damaging effects they can have on girls.
            </p>
            <a class="more show_more_article_text_btn" href="#" id="show_more_article_text_short">
             Show More
            </a>
            <div class="show_less_article_text">
             <p>
              The film stars Lindsay Lohan, Rachel McAdams, Tina Fey, Lacey Chabert, Lizzy Caplan, Daniel Franzese, Jonathan Bennett and Amanda Seyfried (in her film debut).
              <i>
               Saturday Night Live
              </i>
              (
              <i>
               SNL
              </i>
              ) creator Lorne Michaels produced the film. Screenwriter and co-star of the film, Tina Fey, was a long-term cast member and writer for
              <i>
               SNL
              </i>
              . Also featuring appearances from
              <i>
               SNL
              </i>
              cast members Tim Meadows, Ana Gasteyer, and Amy Poehler. The film marks Lohan's second collaboration with director Waters, the
             </p>
             <script type="text/javascript">
              Mediander.Ads.writeDiv('left_more');
             </script>
             <p>
              first being
              <i>
               Freaky Friday
              </i>
              (2003), released a year earlier. Although set in Illinois, the film was mostly shot in Toronto, Canada.
              <br/>
              The film grossed $129 million worldwide and has developed a cult following.
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>
           <!-- /#topic-article -->
           <div class="showless">

             </span>
            </a>
            <a class="less show_less_article_text" href="#">

                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-1">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-1" id="connection-excerpt-1">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Queen Bees and Wannabes
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is a 2002 self-help book by Rosalind Wiseman. It focuses on the ways in which girls in high schools form cliques, and on patterns of aggressive teen girl behavior and how to deal with them. The book was, in large part, the basis for the movie
                   <i>
                    Mean Girls
                   </i>
                   (2004).
                  </p>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-1">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-1" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-1, #show-more-connection-article-1" href="#" id="show-less-1">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
              </div>

               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                Mean Girls
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Queen Bees and Wannabes
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  The book was, in large part, the basis for the movie
                  <i>
                   Mean Girls
                  </i>
                  (2004).
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queen_Bees_and_Wannabes" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Queen Bees and Wannabes
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Tina Fey read Rosalind Wiseman's
                  <i>
                   Queen Bees and Wannabes
                  </i>
                  and called
                  <i>
                   Saturday Night Live
                  </i>
                  producer Lorne Michaels to suggest it could be turned into a film.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_Girls" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Mean Girls
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Mark Waters directed, and Tina Fey wrote the screenplay, which is based in part on Rosalind Wiseman's non-fiction book
                  <i>
                   Queen Bees and Wannabes
                  </i>
                  , which describes female high school social cliques and the damaging effects they can have on girls.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_Girls" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Mean Girls
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-1" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-1" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-1">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-1">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Her
                   <i>
                    New York Times
                   </i>
                   best-selling book
                   <i>
                    Queen Bees and Wannabes: Helping Your Daughter Survive Cliques, Gossip, Boyfriends, and Other Realities of Adolescence,
                   </i>
                   released in 2002, was the basis of the hit comedy film
                   <i>
                    Mean Girls
                   </i>
                   (2004).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rosalind_Wiseman">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Rosalind Wiseman
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The attention this form of aggression has gotten has been augmented by the help of popular media, including movies like
                   <i>
                    Mean Girls
                   </i>
                   and books like
                   <i>
                    Odd Girl Out
                   </i>
                   by R. Simmons (2003), Nesthkchen and the World War by Else Ury (1916), and
                   <i>
                    Queen Bees and Wannabes
                   </i>
                   by R. Wiseman (2003).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relational_aggression">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Relational aggression
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>

                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Rosalind Wiseman
                     </b>
                     is an American parenting educator and author of several publications. Her
                     <i>
                      New York Times
                     </i>
                     best-selling book
                     <i>
                      Queen Bees and Wannabes: Helping Your Daughter Survive Cliques, Gossip, Boyfriends, and Other Realities of Adolescence,
                     </i>
                     released in 2002, was the basis of the hit comedy film
                     <i>
                      Mean Girls
                     </i>
                     (2004). A revised version of
                     <i>
                      Queen Bees and Wannabees
                     </i>
                     was released on October 13, 2009. Wiseman is also the creator of the Owning Up Curriculum, a program that teaches students and educators to take responsibility as bystanders, perpetrators, and victims of unethical behavior.
                    </p>
                   </div>

                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Freaky Friday
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is a 2003 fantasy comedy film based on the novel of the same name by Mary Rodgers. It stars Lindsay Lohan as Anna Coleman and Jamie Lee Curtis as her mother Tess Coleman. In the film their souls are switched due to an enchanted Chinese fortune cookie. It also stars Mark Harmon, Chad Michael Murray, Harold Gould, and Julie Gonzalo. This is Disney's second remake of the original 1976 film starring Barbara Harris and Jodie Foster. A 1995 television remake was produced by ABC, which became a subsidiary of Disney the following year.
                    </p>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-5">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-5" id="connection-excerpt-5">
                   <b>
                    Rachel Anne McAdams
                   </b>
                   (born November 17, 1978) is a Canadian actress. After graduating from a four-year theatre program at York University in 2001, she initially worked in Canadian television and film productions such as the drama film
                   <i>
                    Perfect Pie
                   </i>
                   (2002) (for which she received a Genie Award nomination), the comedy film
                   <i>
                    My Name Is Tanino
                   </i>
                   
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-5 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-5, .show-more-connection-article-5" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-5" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-5-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-5">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Rachel Anne McAdams
                     </b>
                     (born November 17, 1978) is a Canadian actress. After graduating from a four-year theatre program at York University in 2001, she initially worked in Canadian television and film productions such as the drama film
                     <i>
                      Perfect Pie
                     </i>
                     (2002) (for which she received a Genie Award nomination), the comedy film
                     <i>
                      My Name Is Tanino
                     </i>
                     (2002), and the comedy mini-series
                     <i>
                      Slings and Arrows
                     </i>
                     as Kate McNeil (for which she won a Gemini Award). In 2002, she made her Hollywood film debut in the comedy
                     <i>
                      The Hot Chick
                     </i>
                     . McAdams found fame in 2004, co-starring in the comedy
                     <i>
                      Mean Girls
                     </i>
                     and the romantic drama
                     <i>
                      The Notebook
                     </i>
                     . In 2005, she co-starred in the romantic comedy
                     <i>
                      Wedding Crashers
                     </i>
                     , the psychological thriller
                     <i>
                      Red Eye
                     </i>
                     , and the family comedy-drama
                     <i>
                      The Family Stone
                     </i>
                     . She was hailed by the media as Hollywood's new "it girl", and received a BAFTA nomination for Best Rising Star.
                     <br/>
                     McAdams withdrew from the public eye from 2006 to 2007. She made a low-key return to work in 2008, co-starring in two limited release films that were the film noir
                     <i>
                      Married Life
                     </i>
                     and the road trip comedy-drama
                     <i>
                      The Lucky Ones
                     </i>
                     . She returned to prominence in 2009 and co-starred in the political thriller
                     <i>
                      State of Play
                     </i>
                     , the science-fiction romantic drama
                     <i>
                      The Time Traveler's Wife
                     </i>
                     , and the mystery/action-adventure film
                     <i>
                      Sherlock Holmes
                     </i>
                     . In 2010, McAdams co-starred in the comedy
                     <i>
                      Morning Glory
                     </i>
                     , that was billed as her first star vehicle. In 2011, she co-starred in Woody Allen's fantasy romantic comedy
                     <i>
                      Midnight in Paris
                     </i>
                     and reprised her role in the mystery/action-adventure sequel
                     <i>
                      Sherlock Holmes: A Game of Shadows
                     </i>
                     . In 2012, she co-starred in the romantic drama
                     <i>
                      The Vow
                     </i>
                     . In 2013, McAdams co-starred in the romantic drama
                     <i>
                      To the Wonder
                     </i>
                     , the erotic thriller
                     <i>
                      Passion
                     </i>
                     and the romantic comedy-drama
                     <i>
                      About Time
                     </i>
                     . In 2014, she co-starred in the espionage thriller
                     <i>
                      A Most Wanted Man
                     </i>
                     , and in 2015, she co-starred in Wim Wenders's drama
                     <i>
                      Every Thing Will Be Fine
                     </i>
                     and Cameron Crowe's romantic comedy-drama
                     <i>
                      Aloha
                     </i>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     She was inducted into Canada's Walk of Fame in 2014.
                    </p>
                   </div>

                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>

                SHOW MORE

                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-8">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_9_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_9" data-searched="0" data-topic-id="5014081" data-topic-title="Mark Waters (director)" id="jTopicImage_9" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">

                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-8">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-8" id="connection-excerpt-8">
                   <b>
                    Mark Stephen Waters
                   </b>
                   (born June 30, 1964) is an American film director and producer. Waters is perhaps best known for directing
                   <i>
                    Freaky Friday
                   </i>
                   and
                   <i>
                    Mean Girls
                   </i>
                   .
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-8 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-8, .show-more-connection-article-8" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-8" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-8-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-8">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Mark Stephen Waters
                     </b>
                     (born June 30, 1964) is an American film director and producer. Waters is perhaps best known for directing
                     <i>
                      Freaky Friday
                     </i>
                     and
                     <i>
                      Mean Girls
                     </i>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     He is the brother of screenwriter Daniel Waters and has been married to actress Dina Spybey since 2000. He is a graduate of the American Film Institute and as of September 2006 has a development deal with Paramount pictures. He often directs light-hearted, family-friendly films. He has two daughters named Zoe and Alex.
                     <br/>
                     Waters was one of the 120 invitees to join the Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences in 2006.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-8" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-8, #show-more-connection-article-8" href="#" id="show-less-8">

                  </div>

                SHOW MORE
               </a>

               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                Mean Girls
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Mark Waters (director)
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Mark Waters directed, and Tina Fey wrote the screenplay, which is based in part on Rosalind Wiseman's non-fiction book
                  <i>
                   Queen Bees and Wannabes
                  </i>
                  , which describes female high school social cliques and the damaging effects they can have on girls.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_Girls" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Mean Girls
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>

                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-12">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_13_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_13" data-searched="0" data-topic-id="37521774" data-topic-title="Clique" id="jTopicImage_13" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-12">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-12" id="connection-excerpt-12">
                   In the social sciences, a
                   <b>
                    clique
                   </b>
                   (
                   <small>
                    CanE
                   </small>
                   ,
                   <small>
                    UK
                   </small>
                   /klik/ or
                   <small>
                    US
                   </small>
                   /klk/) is a group of people who interact with each other more regularly and intensely than others in the same setting. Interacting with cliques is part of normative social development regardless of gender, ethnicity, or popularity. Although cliques are most commonly studied during adolescence and middle childhood, they exist in all age groups.
                  </p>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-12">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-12" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-12, #show-more-connection-article-12" href="#" id="show-less-12">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                Mean Girls
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Clique
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Mark Waters directed, and Tina Fey wrote the screenplay, which is based in part on Rosalind Wiseman's non-fiction book
                  <i>
                   Queen Bees and Wannabes
                  </i>
                  , which describes female high school social cliques and the damaging effects they can have on girls.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_Girls" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Mean Girls
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  The film also makes references and homages to other films such as when Rick Riker and Trey are in a bus and Trey is pointing out the different groups of cliques, this parodies the
                  <i>
                   Mean Girls
                  </i>
                  scene where Janis explains to Cady the cliques.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superhero_Movie" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Superhero Movie
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Texts -->
             </div>

                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-13" id="connection-excerpt-13">
                   <b>
                    Daniel Franzese
                   </b>
                   (born May 9, 1978) is an American actor. He has worked in film, TV and theater.
                   <br/>
                   Franzese was born in Bensonhurst, Brooklyn, New York, the son of Denise and Ralph "R. J." Franzese, a lounge singer. Franzese attended Piper High School in Sunrise, Florida from 19921996. His mother, Denise, was a lunch lady at Piper and loved by all the students.
                  </p>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-13">

                   <i>
                    Another World
                   </i>
                   for a year when she was 10. At age 11, Lohan made her motion
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-14 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-14, .show-more-connection-article-14" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-14" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-14-short">

                   </span>

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-14">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Lindsay Morgan Lohan
                     </b>
                     (
                     <span>
                      <span>
                       /
                       <span>
                        <span title="// primary stress follows">
                         
                        </span>
                        <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
                         l
                        </span>
                        <span title="/o/ long 'o' in 'code'">
                         o
                        </span>
                        <span title="/./ syllable break">
                         .
                        </span>
                        <span title="/n/ 'on' in 'button'">
                         n
                        </span>
                       </span>
                       /
                      </span>
                     </span>
                     ; born
                     <b>
                      Lindsay Dee Lohan
                     </b>
                     ; July 2, 1986) is an American actress, model, and singer. She began her career as a child fashion model when she was three, and was later featured on the soap opera
                     <i>
                      Another World
                     </i>
                     for a year when she was 10. At age 11, Lohan made her motion picture debut in Disney's remake of
                     <i>
                      The Parent Trap
                     </i>
                     (1998), a critical and commercial success. Her next major motion picture, Disney's remake of
                     <i>
                      Freaky Friday
                     </i>
                     (2003), was also a success at the box office and with critics. With the release of
                     <i>
                      Mean Girls
                     </i>
                     (2004), another critical and commercial success, Lohan became a household name and a frequent focus of paparazzi and tabloids. The two films earned her several MTV Movie Awards and Teen Choice Awards.
                     <br/>
                     Lohan's debut studio album,
                     <i>
                      Speak
                     </i>
                     (2004), was certified platinum. Her second album,
                     <i>
                      A Little More Personal (Raw)
                     </i>
                     (2005), was certified gold. In 2005, Lohan starred in Disney's
                     <i>
                      Herbie: Fully Loaded
                     </i>
                     , another box office success. In 2006, she received positive comments on her work in independent films, including Robert Altman's
                     <i>
                      A Prairie Home Companion
                     </i>
                     and Emilio Estevez's
                     <i>
                      Bobby
                     </i>
                     . In 2007, two driving under the influence incidents led to Lohan being put on probation, and together with three visits to rehabilitation facilities caused the loss of several movie deals.
                     <br/>
                     In 2008 and 2009, Lohan worked as a fashion model and launched the clothing line 6126. She resumed her acting career with TV work in 2008, and starred in the TV film
                     <i>
                      Labor Pains
                     </i>
                     in 2009. She appeared in Robert Rodriguez's feature film
                     <i>
                      Machete
                     </i>
                     (2010). Between 2010 and 2013, Lohan went into rehabilitation three times, and spent much of her time entangled in legal problems stemming from misdemeanors and probation violations. In 2012 and 2013, she did further television work, including starring as Elizabeth Taylor in the biographical TV film
                     <i>
                      Liz &amp; Dick
                     </i>
                     (2012). In 2013, she starred in Paul Schrader's independent film
                     <i>
                      The Canyons
                     </i>
                     . In 2014 the docu-series
                     <i>
                      Lindsay
                     </i>
                     aired on the Oprah Winfrey Network and Lohan made her stage debut in the London West End production of
                     <i>
                      Speed-the-Plow
                     </i>
                     .
                    </p>
                   </div>

                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  17
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-17">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_18_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_18" data-searched="0" data-topic-id="10135555" data-topic-title="Dancing with Myself" id="jTopicImage_18" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-17">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-17" id="connection-excerpt-17">
                   "
                   <b>
                    Dancing with Myself
                   </b>
                   " is a punk rock song written by singer Billy Idol and bassist Tony James, and first recorded by their band Generation X. The song was first released as a single and a 12" in 1980 and, a few weeks after the single release, was included on the band's last album1981's
                   <i>
                    Kiss Me Deadly
                   </i>
                   . It would become one of the group's most well-known songs, but had limited success in its initial release.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-17 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-17, .show-more-connection-article-17" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-17" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-17-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-17">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     "
                     <b>
                      Dancing with Myself
                     </b>
                     " is a punk rock song written by singer Billy Idol and bassist Tony James, and first recorded by their band Generation X. The song was first released as a single and a 12" in 1980 and, a few weeks after the single release, was included on the band's last album1981's
                     <i>
                      Kiss Me Deadly
                     </i>
                     . It would become one of the group's most well-known songs, but had limited success in its initial release.
                     <br/>
                     In 1981, Idol remixed and re-released "Dancing with Myself" as a solo single, toning down its aggressive guitar sound and instead emphasizing its power pop or pop rock elements. Two versions were issuedthe 3:20 single version (which was later included on Idol's
                     <i>
                      11 of the Best
                     </i>
                     compilation), and the 4:50 extended version that appeared on Idol's
                     <i>
                      Don't Stop
                     </i>
                     EP.
                     <br/>
                     Idol plays "Dancing with Myself" at most of his concerts, always introducing the song as having been originally written and recorded by Generation X. Since its release, the song has become something of a sports anthem.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-17" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-17, #show-more-connection-article-17" href="#" id="show-less-17">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-17 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-17" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-17" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-17-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->

                </span>

                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-18 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-18, .show-more-connection-article-18" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-18" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-18-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-18">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Sherway Gardens
                     </b>
                     is a large retail shopping mall in Toronto, Ontario, Canada. The mall is located several kilometres west of downtown Toronto in the former suburb of Etobicoke. Sherway is located near the interchange of Highway 427, Queen Elizabeth Way, and Gardiner Expressway.
                     <br/>
                     The mall opened in 1971. Its original structure covered 850,000 square feet (79,000m
                     <sup>
                      2
                     </sup>
                     ) and contained 127 stores. It was expanded in 1975, 1987 and 1989. Sherway is 972,540 square feet (90,352m
                     <sup>
                      2
                     </sup>
                     ) in size, has 215 stores, and is the eighth largest mall in the Greater Toronto Area.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-18" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-18, #show-more-connection-article-18" href="#" id="show-less-18">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-18 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-18" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-18" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-18-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>

                      30 Rock
                     </i>
                     , a sitcom created by and starring his wife, Tina Fey. He currently executive produces and composes the music for

                     </i>

                    Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel
                   </i>
                   (2009). It was written and produced by Carey, Christopher "Tricky" Stewart and Terius "The-Dream" Nash, and was released as the album's lead single on June 16, 2009. The song draws musical influences from R&amp;B and hip
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-20 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-20, .show-more-connection-article-20" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-20" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-20-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-20">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     "
                     <b>
                      Obsessed
                     </b>
                     " is a song by American singer Mariah Carey from her twelfth studio album,
                     <i>
                      Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel
                     </i>
                     (2009). It was written and produced by Carey, Christopher "Tricky" Stewart and Terius "The-Dream" Nash, and was released as the album's lead single on June 16, 2009. The song draws musical influences from R&amp;B and hip hop music, and is built around a thumping bass line. Additionally, the song is accentuated by hand claps, while Carey's voice is processed with auto-tune. Lyrically, the song describes Mariah's dilemma regarding constant claims of a prior relationship from rapper Eminem, although he is not specifically mentioned.
                     <br/>
                     The song received generally positive reviews from music critics who highlighted it as a stand-out track from
                     <i>
                      Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel
                     </i>
                     . Many reviewers complimented its clever lyrics and strong beat, while others criticized the song's usage of auto-tune on Carey's vocals. At the time of the song's release, "Obsessed" was the center of controversy, as critics and the media suggested Carey was aiming it at American rapper Eminem, who had negatively referenced her several times in songs.
                     <br/>
                     "Obsessed" peaked at number seven on the
                     <i>
                      Billboard
                     </i>
                     Hot 100, becoming Carey's 27th top-ten hit on the chart. In terms of total top-ten chart entries among all artists in the chart's history, Carey tied for fifth place after the song's peak, with Janet Jackson and Elton John. Internationally, the song was not released throughout parts of Europe, as Island Records decided to give priority to the album's second single, Carey's cover of Foreigner's classic "I Want to Know What Love Is". "Obsessed" peaked within the top 10 in France and Italy, and in the top 20 in Australia, Belgium, Canada and Japan.
                     <br/>
                     The song's music video was directed by film-maker Brett Ratner, who Carey has previously worked with on other music videos. Throughout the video, Carey plays both herself and the character of the male stalker, dressed in a bellhop uniform, as well as a gray hoodie and sweatpants. Two videos were shot for "Obsessed", one for the original version, and one for the remixed version, which features rapper Gucci Mane. The video was shot predominantly at the Plaza Hotel, and on the streets of New York City. After several photographs of Carey dressed as the stalker were leaked, tabloids immediately compared Carey's costume to Eminem's usual attire. Carey performed the song live on the fourth season of
                     <i>
                      America's Got Talent
                     </i>
                     ,
                     <i>
                      The Today Show
                     </i>
                     , and throughout her Angels Advocate Tour (200910).
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-20" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-20, #show-more-connection-article-20" href="#" id="show-less-20">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-20 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-20" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-20" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-20-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-21" id="connection-excerpt-21">
                   "
                   <b>
                    Jingle Bell Rock
                   </b>
                   " is a popular Christmas song first released by Bobby Helms in 1957. It has received frequent airplay in the United States during every Christmas season since then. "Jingle Bell Rock" was composed by Joseph Carleton Beal (19001967), and James Ross Boothe (19171976). Beal was a Massachusetts-born public relations professional and longtime resident of South Ocean Avenue in Atlantic City, New Jersey, and Boothe was a Texan writer in the advertising business.
                  </p>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-23">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-23" id="connection-excerpt-23">
                   <b>
                    Teen films
                   </b>
                   is a film genre targeted at teenagers and young adults in which the plot is based upon the special interests of teenagers, such as coming of age, first love, rebellion, conflict with parents, teen angst or alienation. Often these normally serious subject matters are presented in a glossy, stereotyped or trivialized way. For legal reasons, many teenage characters are portrayed by young adults. Some teen films appeal to young males while others appeal to young females.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-23 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-23, .show-more-connection-article-23" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-23" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-23-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-23">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Teen films
                     </b>
                     is a film genre targeted at teenagers and young adults in which the plot is based upon the special interests of teenagers, such as coming of age, first love, rebellion, conflict with parents, teen angst or alienation. Often these normally serious subject matters are presented in a glossy, stereotyped or trivialized way. For legal reasons, many teenage characters are portrayed by young adults. Some teen films appeal to young males while others appeal to young females.
                     <br/>
                     Films in this genre are often set in high schools, or contain characters that are of high school age. Sexual themes are also common, as are crude forms of humor.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-23" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-23, #show-more-connection-article-23" href="#" id="show-less-23">

                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-24 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-24, .show-more-connection-article-24" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-24" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-24-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-24">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Elizabeth Stamatina
                     </b>
                     "
                     <b>
                      Tina
                     </b>
                     "
                     <b>
                      Fey
                     </b>
                     (
                     <span>
                      <span>
                       /
                       <span>
                        <span title="// primary stress follows">
                         
                        </span>
                        <span title="'f' in 'find'">
                         f
                        </span>
                        <span title="/e/ long 'a' in 'base'">
                         e
                        </span>
                       </span>
                       /
                      </span>
                     </span>
                     ; born May 18, 1970) is an American actress, comedian, writer, and producer. She is best known for her work on the NBC sketch comedy series
                     <i>
                      Saturday Night Live
                     </i>
                     (19982006), the creator of
                     <i>
                      30 Rock
                     </i>
                     (20062013) and
                     <i>
                      Unbreakable Kimmy Schmidt
                     </i>
                     (2015present), and films such as
                     <i>
                      Mean Girls
                     </i>
                     (2004),
                     <i>
                      Baby Mama
                     </i>
                     (2008),
                     <i>
                      Date Night
                     </i>
                     (2010), and
                     <i>
                      Muppets Most Wanted
                     </i>
                     (2014).
                     <br/>
                     Fey broke into comedy as a featured player in the Chicago-based improvisational comedy group The Second City. She then joined
                     <i>
                      SNL
                     </i>
                     as a writer, later becoming head writer and a performer, known for her position as co-anchor in the
                     <i>
                      Weekend Update
                     </i>
                     segment. In 2004, she co-starred in and wrote the screenplay for
                     <i>
                      Mean Girls,
                     </i>
                     which was adapted from the 2002 self-help book
                     <i>
                      Queen Bees and Wannabes
                     </i>
                     . After leaving
                     <i>
                      SNL
                     </i>
                     in 2006, she created the television series
                     <i>
                      30 Rock
                     </i>
                     for Broadway Video, a situation comedy loosely based on her experiences at
                     <i>
                      SNL
                     </i>
                     . In the series, Fey portrays the head writer of a fictional sketch comedy series. In 2008, she starred in the comedy film
                     <i>
                      Baby Mama
                     </i>
                     , alongside former
                     <i>
                      SNL
                     </i>
                     co-star Amy Poehler. Fey next appeared in the 2010 comedy film
                     <i>
                      Date Night
                     </i>
                     and the animated film
                     <i>
                      Megamind
                     </i>
                     . In 2015, she created and produced the television series
                     <i>
                      Unbreakable Kimmy Schmidt
                     </i>
                     for NBC, although it was eventually moved to Netflix.
                     <br/>
                     Fey has received eight Emmy Awards, two Golden Globe Awards, five Screen Actors Guild Awards, and four Writers Guild of America Awards, and has been nominated for a Grammy Award for her autobiographical book
                     <i>
                      Bossypants
                     </i>
                     , which topped the The New York Times Best Seller list for five weeks. In 2008, the Associated Press gave Fey the AP Entertainer of the Year award for her satirical portrayal of Republican vice presidential candidate Sarah Palin in a guest appearance on
                     <i>
                      SNL
                     </i>
                     . In 2010, Fey was the recipient of the Mark Twain Prize for American Humor, the youngest-ever winner of the award. On January 13, 2013, Fey hosted the 70th Golden Globe Awards with her long-time friend and fellow comedian, Amy Poehler. Their performance was critically acclaimed. The duo hosted again the following two years, generating the highest ratings for the annual ceremony in a decade.
                    </p>

            <li class="connection" data-id="7220211" data-original-title='"Naughty Girl" is a song recorded by American singer Beyonc from her debut studio album, Dangerously in Love' data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="naughty-girl-%28beyonc%C3%A9-song%29" id="7220211" title="">

               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">

                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-26">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_27_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_27" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="7220211" data-topic-title="Naughty Girl (Beyonc song)" id="jTopicImage_27" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d0/Beyonce_-_Naughty_Girl_single_cover.jpg/128px-Beyonce_-_Naughty_Girl_single_cover.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-26">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-26" id="connection-excerpt-26">
                   "
                   <b>
                    Naughty Girl
                   </b>
                   " is a song recorded by American singer Beyonc from her debut studio album,
                   <i>
                    Dangerously in Love
                   </i>
                   (2003). It was written by Robert Waller, Angela Beyinc, Scott Storch and Knowles, and produced by the Storch and Beyinc. The song was released by Columbia Records as the fourth and final single from the album to
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-26 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-26, .show-more-connection-article-26" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-26" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-26-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-26">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     "
                     <b>
                      Naughty Girl
                     </b>
                     " is a song recorded by American singer Beyonc from her debut studio album,
                     <i>
                      Dangerously in Love
                     </i>
                     (2003). It was written by Robert Waller, Angela Beyinc, Scott Storch and Knowles, and produced by the Storch and Beyinc. The song was released by Columbia Records as the fourth and final single from the album to US radios on March 14, 2004, and was available as a physical release the next month. An official remix featuring Lil Kim was released in the following month, as well. Musically, "Naughty Girl" is an R&amp;B and disco song that interpolates from the Donna Summer's song, "Love to Love You Baby" (1975). Influenced by Arabic music, dancehall and reggae, the song contains lyrics that reference to a celebration of sexual lust and conquest, leading up to a desire for a one-night stand.
                     <br/>
                     "Naughty Girl" was received with positive reviews by music critics, who praised Knowles' assertive vocals and the song's sensual vibe. However, opinions about how convincingly Knowles was able to portray a naughty girl were polarized. The song was nominated in the category Best R&amp;B/Soul Single by a Female Artist at the 2005 Soul Train Music Awards. "Naughty Girl" peaked at number three on the US
                     <i>
                      Billboard
                     </i>
                     Hot 100, becoming Knowles' fourth consecutive release from the album to reach the top five on that chart. The single reached the top ten in New Zealand, Australia, the Netherlands and the United Kingdom. "Naughty Girl" was certified gold by the American, Australian and New Zealander trade associations of record producers.
                     <br/>
                     The single's accompanying music video was directed by Jake Nava and was inspired by the dancing of Cyd Charisse and Fred Astaire in the 1953 musical comedy film,
                     <i>
                      The Band Wagon
                     </i>
                     . In it, Knowles flirtatiously and seductively dances with R&amp;B singer Usher to portray a naughty girl. The video received four nominations at the 2004 MTV Video Music Awards and eventually won the Best Female Video accolade. The song was included on Knowles' set lists on her tours. The American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers (ASCAP) recognized "Naughty Girl" as one of the most performed songs of 2005 at the ASCAP Pop Music Awards. "Naughty Girl" has been covered by singer-songwriter Roesy and band Richard Cheese and Lounge Against the Machine.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-26" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-26, #show-more-connection-article-26" href="#" id="show-less-26">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-26 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-26" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-26" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-26-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                <li>

                  "Naughty Girl" was also used in the trailer for the 2004 Paramount Pictures film "Mean Girls".
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naughty_Girl_%28Beyonc%C3%A9_song%29" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Naughty Girl (Beyonc song)
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Though not included on the soundtrack, other songs heard in the film include the single "Pass That Dutch" by Missy Elliott, "Naughty Girl" by Beyonc, "Beautiful" by Christina Aguilera, "Fire" by Joe Budden featuring Busta Rhymes, "At Seventeen" by Janis Ian, and "Halcyon + On + On" by Orbital and "Love's Theme" by The Love Unlimited Orchestra.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_Girls" target="_blank">
                   from

                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>

                 <div class="connection-counter">

                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-27">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_28_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_28" data-searched="0" data-topic-id="2781104" data-topic-title="Convocation Hall (University of Toronto)" id="jTopicImage_28" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-27">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-27" id="connection-excerpt-27">
                   <b>
                    Convocation Hall
                   </b>
                   is a domed rotunda on the grounds of the University of Toronto in Toronto, Ontario, Canada. Designed by Pearson and Darling and completed in 1907, it was inspired by the grand theatre of the Sorbonne and the Sheldonian Theatre at Oxford. While the building's namesake purpose is to host the annual convocation ceremonies, it also serves as the venue for academic and social functions that involve large audiences throughout the year.
                  </p>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-27">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-27" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-27, #show-more-connection-article-27" href="#" id="show-less-27">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
              </div>

                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-29 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-29, .show-more-connection-article-29" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-29" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-29-short">

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-29">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Brittney Rose "Nikki" Cleary
                     </b>
                     (born May 11, 1988, Albany, New York) is an American pop-rock singer.
                     <br/>
                     Cleary first hit the pop market with the song "I.M. Me" while still using her given name. Her debut album,
                     <i>
                      Everything I Wished For
                     </i>
                     , was released independently under the Free Falls record label in 2002 after two years of recording. The album hit #45 on Billboard's Top Independent Albums chart. When Cleary signed with Jive Records in the summer of 2002, they asked to change her name because they already had a Britney on their roster. Her self-titled album,
                     <i>
                      Nikki Cleary
                     </i>
                     was released in the summer of 2003.
                     <br/>
                     She was featured on a Nickelodeon Kids' Choice Awards record in 2003, with her single "1,2,3". She also performed on Nickelodeon's "All That." Cleary also did a version of "Summertime Guys", featured on the Kim Possible soundtrack. She contributed to the
                     <i>
                      Mean Girls
                     </i>
                     motion picture soundtrack with the song "Hated".
                     <br/>
                     Nikki attended Clayton A. Bouton High School in Voorheesville, New York, and Mohonasen's Draper Middle School in Schenectady, New York. She was married in the summer of 2009, and has four children.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-29" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-29, #show-more-connection-article-29" href="#" id="show-less-29">

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-31">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-31" id="connection-excerpt-31">
                   <b>
                    The Love Unlimited Orchestra
                   </b>
                   , formed by American R&amp;B/soul musician Barry White, was a 40-piece string-laden orchestra that served as a backing unit for Barry White and female vocal trio Love Unlimited. From the early 1970s on, they also recorded several singles and albums under their own name.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-31 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-31, .show-more-connection-article-31" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-31" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-31-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-31">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      The Love Unlimited Orchestra
                     </b>
                     , formed by American R&amp;B/soul musician Barry White, was a 40-piece string-laden orchestra that served as a backing unit for Barry White and female vocal trio Love Unlimited. From the early 1970s on, they also recorded several singles and albums under their own name.
                     <br/>
                     Their biggest hit single was 1973's instrumental disc, "Love's Theme". The track, written by Barry White, went to No. 1 for one week in the U.S. and No. 10 in the UK Singles Chart. The R.I.A.A. awarded a gold disc on 7 February 1974.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-31" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-31, #show-more-connection-article-31" href="#" id="show-less-31">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-31 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-31" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-31" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-31-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                Mean Girls
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                The Love Unlimited Orchestra
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Though not included on the soundtrack, other songs heard in the film include the single "Pass That Dutch" by Missy Elliott, "Naughty Girl" by Beyonc, "Beautiful" by Christina Aguilera, "Fire" by Joe Budden featuring Busta Rhymes, "At Seventeen" by Janis Ian, and "Halcyon + On + On" by Orbital and "Love's Theme" by The Love Unlimited Orchestra.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_Girls" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Mean Girls
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
              </div>

                     "
                     <b>
                      Pass That Dutch
                     </b>
                     " is a song by American recording artist Missy Elliott. It was written and produced by Timbaland and Elliott for her fifth studio album
                     <i>
                      This Is Not A Test!
                     </i>
                     (2003) and contains samples of Santa Esmeralda's version of "Don't Let Me Be Misunderstood", "Magic Mountain" by War, and "Potholes in My Lawn" by De La Soul. Released as the album's lead single in October 2003, the song reached number 9 on
                     <i>
                      Billboard
                     </i>
                     's Rap Songs chart and number 27 on the Hot 100 . In addition, it peaked at number ten in United Kingdom and reached the top 20 in Finland and Norway.
                     <br/>
                     The song was ranked first in MuchMusic's "Top 50 MuchVibe Videos of All Time" countdown and 291st on Pitchfork Media's "Top 500 songs of the 2000s". "Pass That Dutch" was also featured in the movie,
                     <i>
                      Mean Girls
                     </i>
                     , but is not on the soundtrack.
                    </p>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-35">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-35" id="connection-excerpt-35">
                   "
                   <b>
                    At Seventeen
                   </b>
                   " is a song by Janis Ian, released in 1975 on
                   <i>
                    Between the Lines
                   </i>
                   (her seventh studio album) and as a single. Ian's most successful recording, the song is a commentary on adolescent cruelty, the illusion of popularity, and teenage angst, as reflected upon from the maturity of adulthood. It is told from the point of view of a woman who was an "ugly duckling" as a girl and ignored in high school while the popular girls got all the attention.
                  </p>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-35">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-35" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-35, #show-more-connection-article-35" href="#" id="show-less-35">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_Girls" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>

                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>

            <li class="connection" data-id="7044185" data-original-title="&quot;Love's Theme&quot; is an instrumental piece recorded by Barry White's Love Unlimited Orchestra and released in 1973 as" data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="love%27s-theme" id="7044185" title="">
             <a data-topic-id="7044185" href="#!/7044185/love%27s-theme">
              <ol class="post-list">
               <li>
                <div class="connection-counter">
                 36
                </div>
                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="0" data-topic-id="7044185" data-topic-title="Love's Theme" id="jTopicImage_37" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                 <div class="connection-title-and-excerpt">
                  <span class="connection-title" data-count="36" data-id="7044185" data-url-title="love%27s-theme">
                   Love's Theme
                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   "Love's Theme" is an instrumental piece recorded by Barry White's Love Unlimited Orchestra and released in 1973 as
                  </span>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </li>
              </ol>
             </a>
            </li>
            <!-- /Collapsed connection -->
            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="7044185" data-url-title="love%27s-theme" id="connection-expanded-36">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  36
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-36">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_37_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_37" data-searched="0" data-topic-id="7044185" data-topic-title="Love's Theme" id="jTopicImage_37" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-36">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-36" id="connection-excerpt-36">
                   "
                   <b>
                    Love's Theme
                   </b>
                   " is an instrumental piece recorded by Barry White's Love Unlimited Orchestra and released in 1973 as an A-Side single. It is one of the few instrumental and purely orchestral singles to reach number one on the
                   <i>
                    Billboard
                   </i>
                   Hot 100 chart in the United States, which it did in early 1974.
                   <i>
                    Billboard
                   </i>
                   ranked it
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-36 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-36, .show-more-connection-article-36" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-36" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-36-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-36">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     "
                     <b>
                      Love's Theme
                     </b>
                     " is an instrumental piece recorded by Barry White's Love Unlimited Orchestra and released in 1973 as an A-Side single. It is one of the few instrumental and purely orchestral singles to reach number one on the
                     <i>
                      Billboard
                     </i>
                     Hot 100 chart in the United States, which it did in early 1974.
                     <i>
                      Billboard
                     </i>
                     ranked it as the No. 3 song for 1974. The piece was included on two albums: 1973's
                     <i>
                      Under the Influence of... Love Unlimited
                     </i>
                     (by the vocal group
                     <i>
                      Love Unlimited
                     </i>
                     ) and 1974's
                     <i>
                      Rhapsody in White
                     </i>
                     by Love Unlimited Orchestra.
                     <br/>
                     The recording, with a large string orchestra, wah-wah guitar, and big rhythm, is considered by author Peter Shapiro to be an influence to the disco sound, which would explode in popularity the following year. The song was also popular on the Adult Contemporary chart in the U.S., where the song spent two weeks at #1. It was also used by ABC Sports for many years as the opening theme music for its golf coverage. In Canada, the single saw similar success, reaching #1 on the
                     <i>
                      RPM 100
                     </i>
                     National Singles Chart on March 2, 1974.
                     <br/>
                     In addition, "Love's Theme" was also recorded in a vocal version by Love Unlimited (on their 1974 album
                     <i>
                      In Heat
                     </i>
                     ), . Enoch Light recorded an electro-disco instrumental version of the song on his 1977 album,
                     <i>
                      Disco Disque
                     </i>
                     . The song is also part of Meco's instrumental medley "Hooked On Instrumentals Part I" (from the 1985 album
                     <i>
                      Hooked On Instrumentals
                     </i>
                     ). In May 1993, Orchestral Manoeuvres in the Dark released the single "Dream of Me (Based on Love's Theme)" (from their album
                     <i>
                      Liberator
                     </i>
                     , released the same year) which used a sample of this Barry White composition. This single reached #24 on the UK Singles Chart, and Barry White was given a writing credit.
                     <br/>
                     This song was covered by American smooth jazz trumpeter Rick Braun and by American guitarist Chuck Loeb.
                     <br/>
                     The Hong Kong-based Cathay Pacific Airways used the song for their TV advertisements. It was also featured briefly in
                     <i>
                      Mean Girls
                     </i>
                     ,
                     <i>
                      Despicable Me 2
                     </i>
                     and
                     <i>

                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-39 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-39, .show-more-connection-article-39" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-39" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-39-short">

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-39">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Joe Budden
                     </b>
                     (born August 31, 1980) is an American hip hop recording artist from Jersey City, New Jersey, who, in addition to being a solo artist, is a member of the American hip hop supergroup Slaughterhouse, alongside fellow rappers Royce da 5'9", Joell Ortiz, and Crooked I.
                     <br/>
                     His most commercially successful single is the 2003 hit song "Pump It Up", from his self-titled album, which contains production from Just Blaze. He was formerly signed to major record label Def Jam, but left for personal reasons and for them pushing back his album releases. After his splitting from Def Jam, he began recording and releasing mixtapes and albums on independent labels. He released
                     <i>
                      No Love Lost
                     </i>
                     (2013). Then most recently on Nov 4, 2014 he released Some Love Lost. Budden also co-stars on the VH1 reality show
                     <i>
                      Love &amp; Hip Hop
                     </i>
                     .
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-39" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-39, #show-more-connection-article-39" href="#" id="show-less-39">

                   </a>
                  </div>

                   <b>
                    Montclair High School
                   </b>
                   is a comprehensive four-year public high school located in Montclair, in Essex County, New Jersey, United States, serving students in ninth through twelfth grades as the lone secondary school of the Montclair Public Schools. The school has been accredited by the Middle States Association of Colleges and Schools Commission on Secondary Schools since 1928.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-42 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-42, .show-more-connection-article-42" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-42" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-42-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-42">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Montclair High School
                     </b>
                     is a comprehensive four-year public high school located in Montclair, in Essex County, New Jersey, United States, serving students in ninth through twelfth grades as the lone secondary school of the Montclair Public Schools. The school has been accredited by the Middle States Association of Colleges and Schools Commission on Secondary Schools since 1928.
                     <br/>
                     As of the 2012-13 school year, the school had an enrollment of 1,969 students and 157.6 classroom teachers (on an FTE basis), for a studentteacher ratio of 12.50:1. There were 302 students (15.3% of enrollment) eligible for free lunch and 93 (4.7% of students) eligible for reduced-cost lunch.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-42" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-42, #show-more-connection-article-42" href="#" id="show-less-42">

                   </a>
                  </div>

                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-44 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-44, .show-more-connection-article-44" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-44" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-44-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
