                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-44">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     "
                     <b>
                      Milkshake
                     </b>
                     " is a song by American recording artist Kelis and the lead single from her third studio album,
                     <i>
                      Tasty
                     </i>
                     . The song was released in the United States on August 25, 2003, by Star Trak and Arista Records, and internationally on November 24. It was written and produced by The Neptunes, a duo that had made the majority of Kelis' songs in the past. According to Kelis, "milkshake" in the song is used as a metaphor for "something that makes women special." The song is noted for its euphemistic chorus and low beat R&amp;B sound.
                     <br/>
                     The song peaked at number three on the US
                     <i>
                      Billboard
                     </i>
                     Hot 100 chart in December, 2003, becoming Kelis' best charting single in the country to this day. The song achieved commercial success internationally, as it topped the chart in Ireland, and peaked inside the top three in Australia, New Zealand and the United Kingdom. "Milkshake" was certified gold in the United States, where it has sold 883,000 paid downloads. The song was nominated for a Grammy Award for Best Urban/Alternative Performance in 2004.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-44" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-44, #show-more-connection-article-44" href="#" id="show-less-44">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-44 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-44" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-44" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-44-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-46 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-46, .show-more-connection-article-46" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-46" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-46-short">

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-46">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Tony Blondal
                     </b>
                     , is a film and television orchestrator and conductor, and record arranger. He started out his musical career playing live (guitar) and doing studio recording sessions (guitar, mandolin, banjo, balalaika, charango and various instruments). He also pursued his other interests, which were writing orchestral and band arrangements for singers, and big band writing and arranging. Through this early work he met a group of TV composers who were busy and needed someone to help orchestrate and copy their music for weekly recording sessions. That experience led to other opportunities and started him on a new path, and he soon transitioned to film orchestration. To this day he still works in film primarily, but also occasionally in television and video games.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-46" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-46, #show-more-connection-article-46" href="#" id="show-less-46">

                   </a>

The final choice was made in part because Malia Obama's allergies dictated a need for a hypoallergenic breed. Bo has occasionally been called "First Dog". In August 2013 Bo was joined by Sunny, a female dog of the same breed.

                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-49 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-49, .show-more-connection-article-49" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-49" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-49-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-49">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Malvern Collegiate Institute
                     </b>
                     is a Toronto high school that was founded in 1903 as "East Toronto High School", in what was then the village of East Toronto. When the village was annexed by Toronto in 1908, the name of the street the school was located on was changed from Charles Street to Malvern Avenue (as Toronto already had a Charles Street), and the name of the institution was changed shortly thereafter.
                     <br/>
                     The statue that stands on the east side of the school on Malvern Avenue just outside of the library was built in 1922 in honour of the students that had attended Malvern C.I. and died in World War I.
                     <br/>
                     Malvern Collegiate is located in an upper-middle-class neighbourhood known as The Beaches. Notable alumni include Glenn Gould, Robert Fulford, and Don Getty who were all at the school at the same time in the 1950s. Norman Jewison, Bruce Kidd, Teresa Stratas and Jack Kent Cooke also attended the school.
                     <br/>
                     Malvern celebrated its centennial in 2003. In 2006,
                     <i>
                      Toronto Life
                     </i>
                     magazine stated that Malvern CI had the best English program in Toronto, a notable change from the 1980s, when the same magazine rated Malvern's English department as being in the bottom five of all Toronto collegiates. The school's mascot is the Black Knight, and the school colours are red and black.
                     <br/>
                     Coincidentally, there is also a Toronto neighbourhood called Malvern, but the school and the neighbourhood share no connection. The Malvern neighbourhood is located approximately 16km (9.9mi) northeast of Malvern Collegiate.
                     <br/>
                     Malvern won the 2009 Anne Hope Award for its contributions in promoting human rights and equity education.
                     <br/>
                     In November, 2011, a ceremony rededicating the statue located on the east side of the school was held, a week before Remembrance Day of that year to commemorate the repairs done to the arm. Less than 48 hours later, the statue was vandalized.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-49" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-49, #show-more-connection-article-49" href="#" id="show-less-49">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-49 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-49" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-49" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-49-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->

               <!-- Connection Texts -->

                </span>

                <br/>
                <span>

                </span>

               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Although set in Evanston, Illinois, the film was mostly shot in Toronto, Ontario, Canada at Etobicoke Collegiate Institute and Malvern Collegiate Institute as well as Montclair, New Jersey at Montclair High School.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_Girls" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>

                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>

            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="1696008" data-url-title="beautiful-%28christina-aguilera-so" id="connection-expanded-50">

                <li>

                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-50">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_51_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_51" data-searched="0" data-topic-id="1696008" data-topic-title="Beautiful (Christina Aguilera song)" id="jTopicImage_51" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-50">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-50" id="connection-excerpt-50">
                   "
                   <b>
                    Beautiful
                   </b>
                   " is a song recorded by American singer Christina Aguilera on her fourth studio album,
                   <i>
                    Stripped
                   </i>
                   . It was released as the album's second single on November 16, 2002. A pop ballad, "Beautiful" was written and produced by Linda Perry. Lyrically, it discusses inner beauty, as well as self-esteem and insecurity issues. Aguilera commented that she
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-50 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-50, .show-more-connection-article-50" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-50" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-50-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-50">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     "
                     <b>
                      Beautiful
                     </b>
                     " is a song recorded by American singer Christina Aguilera on her fourth studio album,
                     <i>
                      Stripped
                     </i>
                     . It was released as the album's second single on November 16, 2002. A pop ballad, "Beautiful" was written and produced by Linda Perry. Lyrically, it discusses inner beauty, as well as self-esteem and insecurity issues. Aguilera commented that she put "her heart and her soul" into the track, which she felt represented the theme of
                     <i>
                      Stripped
                     </i>
                     . The song was later re-recorded in an electronic style for her first greatest hits album
                     <i>
                      Keeps Gettin' Better: A Decade of Hits
                     </i>
                     (2008).
                     <br/>
                     Upon its release, "Beautiful" received universal acclaim from music critics, who have ranked it among Aguilera's strongest material. It won a Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance and was also nominated for Song of the Year at the 2004 ceremony. "Beautiful" was also a commercial success, topping the charts in Australia, Belgium, Canada, Ireland, New Zealand and the United Kingdom. The song peaked at number two on the
                     <i>
                      Billboard
                     </i>
                     Hot 100 in the United States, where it was certified gold for 500,000 units shipped.
                     <br/>
                     "Beautiful" has been widely embraced as an anthem by the LGBT community for its message of self-empowerment and inner beauty. An accompanying music video was directed by Jonas kerlund, and earned Aguilera a GLAAD Media Award for its positive portrayal of gay and transgender people. In 2011, UK LGBT rights organization Stonewall named "Beautiful" the most empowering song of the previous decade for gay, lesbian, and bisexual people. In 2009,
                     <i>
                      Rolling Stone
                     </i>
                     and VH1 listed it as one of the best songs of the 2000s. The song is widely recognized as one of Aguilera's signature songs and has been covered on numerous occasions and featured on several television shows.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-50" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-50, #show-more-connection-article-50" href="#" id="show-less-50">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                   from
                   <span>
                    Mean Girls
